## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Solid Mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the thermo-mechanical constitutive relationship of materials, predicting stress (sigma) as a function of mechanical deformation (epsilon) and thermal state (T). The underlying physics typically involves linear elasticity, plastic strain hardening, yield point transitions, and temperature-dependent softening or thermal strain compensation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic deformation regime)
- Thermal strain compensation: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress corrected for thermal expansion/contraction)
- Ludwik strain hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic work hardening behavior)
- Swift hardening law: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (offset strain hardening with pre-strain)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (flow stress approaching dynamic recovery asymptote)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-modulated elasticity and hardening)
- Johnson-Cook multiplicative model: sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) * (c4 + c5 * T) (decoupled strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) * exp(c4 * T) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence of flow stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic proportionality → Direct linear scaling c * epsilon (Hookean regime)
- Plastic strain hardening → Power-law or exponential growth c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (work hardening)
- Flow stress saturation → Exponential asymptote c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (dynamic recovery)
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative decay factor (1 + c * T) or exp(c * T) reducing stress magnitude
- Thermal strain offset → Linear variable shift (epsilon - c * T) accounting for expansion/contraction
- Elastoplastic transition → Bilinear hinge function c1 * epsilon + c2 * Max(epsilon - c3, 0) (yield point)
- Thermo-mechanical coupling → Bilinear interaction term c * T * epsilon modifying tangent stiffness

The user wants me to identify which of the 57 candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)`
GT numerical expression: `96.82940277854249*epsilon*(-0.00975241411319901*(T - 352.18178394696326) + 1) - 0.4784822007985676*(T - 352.18178394696326) + 8.062014375498787*(T - 352.18178394696326)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let's simplify the GT expression algebraically.
Let $T_0 = c2 = c5 = c7 = 352.18178394696326$.
Let $A = c0 = 96.82940277854249$.
Let $B = c1 = 0.00975241411319901$.
Let $C = c3 = 1$.
Let $D = c4 = 0.4784822007985676$.
Let $E = c6 = 8.062014375498787$.
Let $F = c8 = 1$.

GT = $A \cdot \epsilon \cdot (-B \cdot (T - T_0) + C) - D \cdot (T - T_0) + E \cdot (T - T_0) \cdot \log(\epsilon + F)$
GT = $-A B \epsilon (T - T_0) + A C \epsilon - D (T - T_0) + E (T - T_0) \log(\epsilon + F)$
GT = $(T - T_0) \cdot [ -A B \epsilon - D + E \log(\epsilon + F) ] + A C \epsilon$

Let's group terms by $T$ and constants:
GT = $T \cdot [ -A B \epsilon - D + E \log(\epsilon + F) ] + T_0 \cdot [ A B \epsilon + D - E \log(\epsilon + F) ] + A C \epsilon$
GT = $T \cdot [ E \log(\epsilon + F) - A B \epsilon - D ] + [ T_0 (A B \epsilon + D - E \log(\epsilon + F)) + A C \epsilon ]$

So the GT is a linear function of $T$: $GT = P(\epsilon) \cdot T + Q(\epsilon)$.
Where:
$P(\epsilon) = E \log(\epsilon + F) - A B \epsilon - D$
$Q(\epsilon) = T_0 (A B \epsilon + D - E \log(\epsilon + F)) + A C \epsilon$

Notice that $Q(\epsilon) = -T_0 P(\epsilon) + A C \epsilon$.
So $GT = P(\epsilon) (T - T_0) + A C \epsilon$.
This matches the original form: $(T - T_0) [ E \log(\epsilon + F) - A B \epsilon - D ] + A C \epsilon$.

Key features of GT:
- Linear in $T$.
- Contains $\log(\epsilon + F)$ multiplied by $(T - T_0)$.
- Contains $\epsilon$ multiplied by $(T - T_0)$.
- Contains constant term (w.r.t $T$) proportional to $\epsilon$.
- No exponentials, no trigonometric functions, no powers of $T$ other than $T^1$.
- Structure: $T \cdot (\text{function of } \epsilon) + (\text{function of } \epsilon)$.

Let's look at the candidates. They are mostly rational functions or sums of terms.
Many candidates have the form `(Numerator) / (Denominator)`.
If a candidate is a rational function in $T$, say $N(T, \epsilon) / D(T, \epsilon)$, for it to be linear in $T$, the denominator must cancel out the $T$ dependence in the numerator, or the denominator must be independent of $T$, or the whole expression simplifies to linear in $T$.

Let's check each candidate systematically.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`GT = c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)`
Expanding and grouping by `T`:
`GT = T * [ c6*log(epsilon + c8) - c0*c1*epsilon - c4 ] + [ c0*epsilon*(c1*c2 + c3) + c4*c5 - c6*c7*log(epsilon + c8) ]`
**Key Structural Features:**
1. **Linear in `T`**: The expression is strictly of the form `P(epsilon)*T + Q(epsilon)`.
2. **Coefficient of `T`**: Contains a logarithmic term `log(epsilon + c8)` multiplied by `T`, plus linear and constant terms in `epsilon`.
3. **Basis Functions**: Only polynomials in `epsilon`, `log(epsilon + const)`, and linear `T`. No exponentials, trigonometric functions, or powers of `T` other than `T^1`.

### Candidate Analysis
**Candidate 1:** Contains `log(T*c7 + 1)`. This is logarithmic in `T`, not linear. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 2:** Simplifies to `A/(c3*T + c4) + B(epsilon)`. Rational in `T`, not linear. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 3:** Contains `log(T*c7 + 1)`. Logarithmic in `T`. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 4:** Contains `T**c0`. Unless `c0=1`, non-linear. Even if `c0=1`, the coefficient of `T` is constant, while GT's coefficient depends on `epsilon`. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 5:** Coefficient of `T` is `c0*sin(c2*epsilon + c3)`. Bounded sine cannot match unbounded `log(epsilon) + linear`. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 6:** Contains `log(c2*exp(T*c3) + 1)`. Softplus-like function of `T`, not linear. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 7:** Coefficient of `T` is `c1/(c3*epsilon + c4)`. Rational function of `epsilon` cannot match `log(epsilon) + linear`. `[NO MATCH]`
